3407     /**
3408      * Produces a method handle giving write access to elements of an array,
3409      * as if by the {@code astore} bytecode.
3410      * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3411      * Its last argument will be the array's element type.
3412      * The first and second arguments will be the array type and int.
3413      *
3414      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3415      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3416      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3417      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3418      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3419      * the length of the array.
3420      *
3421      * @param arrayClass the class of an array
3422      * @return a method handle which can store values into the array type
3423      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3424      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3425      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aastore} Instruction
3426      */
3427     public static MethodHandle arrayElementSetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3428         if (arrayClass.isInlineClass()) {
3429             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
3430         }
3431         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.SET);
3432     }
3433 
3434     /**
3435      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
3436      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
3437      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3438      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3439      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
3440      * <p>
3441      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3442      * the following conditions:
3443      * <ul>
3444      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
3445      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3446      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
3447      *     modes are unsupported.
3448      * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3449      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3450      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3451      *     unsupported.
3452      * </ul>
3453      * <p>
3454      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3455      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3456      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3457      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3458      *
3459      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
3460      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3461      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3462      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3463      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3464      * the length of the array.
3465      *
3466      * @apiNote
3467      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3468      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3469      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3470      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3471      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3472      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3473      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3474      * unexpectedly fail.
3475      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3476      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3477      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3478      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3479      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3480      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3481      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3482      * details).
3483      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3484      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3485      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3486      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3487      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3488      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
3489      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
3490      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
3491      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3492      * @since 9
3493      */
3494     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3495         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
3496     }
3497 
3498     /**
3499      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
3500      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
3501      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
3502      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
3503      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3504      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3505      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
3506      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
3507      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
3508      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
3509      * <p>
3510      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
3511      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
3512      * {@code double}.
3513      * <p>
3514      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
3515      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
3516      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
3517      * of {@code T}.
3518      * <p>
3519      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
3520      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
3521      * with the array and index.
3522      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
3523      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
3524      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
3525      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
3526      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
3527      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
3528      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
3529      * <ul>
3530      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
3531      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
3532      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
3533      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
3534      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
3535      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3536      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3537      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
3538      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3539      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3540      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
3541      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3542      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3543      * </ul>
3544      * <p>
3545      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
3546      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
3547      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
3548      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
3549      * <pre>{@code
3550      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
3551      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
3552      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
3553      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
3554      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
3555      * }</pre>
3556      * <p>
3557      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
3558      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
3559      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3560      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3561      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
3562      * type {@code T}
3563      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
3564      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
3565      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
3566      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
3567      * array class
3568      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
3569      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
3570      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
3571      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
3572      * @since 9
3573      */
3574     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
3575                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3576         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
3577         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
3578                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
3579     }
3580 
3581     /**
3582      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
3583      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
3584      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
3585      * {@code long[]}.
3586      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
3587      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3588      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3589      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
3590      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
3591      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
3592      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
3593      * <p>
3594      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
3595      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
3596      * {@code double}.
3597      * <p>
3598      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
3599      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
3600      * <p>
3601      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
3602      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
3603      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
3604      * {@code T}.
3605      * <p>
3606      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
3607      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
3608      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
3609      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
3610      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
3611      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
3612      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
3613      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
3614      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
3615      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
3616      * <ul>
3617      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
3618      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
3619      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
3620      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
3621      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
3622      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3623      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3624      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
3625      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3626      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3627      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
3628      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
3629      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
3630      * </ul>
3631      * <p>
3632      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
3633      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
3634      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
3635      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
3636      * <pre>{@code
3637      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
3638      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
3639      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
3640      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
3641      * }</pre>
3642      * <p>
3643      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
3644      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
3645      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3646      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3647      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
3648      * type {@code T}
3649      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
3650      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
3651      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
3652      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
3653      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
3654      * array class
3655      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
3656      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
3657      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
3658      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
3659      * @since 9
3660      */
3661     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
3662                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3663         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
3664         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
3665                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
3666     }

3668 
3669     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
3670 
3671     /**
3672      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
3673      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
3674      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
3675      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
3676      * arguments:
3677      * <ul>
3678      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
3679      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
3680      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
3681      * </ul>
3682      * <p>
3683      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
3684      * the indicated {@code type}.
3685      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
3686      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
3687      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
3688      * <p>
3689      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
3690      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
3691      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
3692      * the final parameter.
3693      * <p>
3694      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
3695      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
3696      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
3697      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
3698      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
3699      * <p>
3700      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
3701      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
3702 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
3703 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
3704 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
3705 return invoker;
3706      * }</pre></blockquote>
3707      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
3708      * @param type the desired target type
3709      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
3710      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
3711      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
3712      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
3713      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
3714      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
3715      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
3716      */
3717     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
3718         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
3719             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
3720         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
3721         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
3722     }
3723 
3724     /**
3725      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
3726      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
3727      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
3728      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
3729      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
3730      * <p>
3731      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
3732      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
3733      *
3734      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
3735      * <em>Discussion:</em>
3736      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
3737      * of unknown types.
3738      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
3739      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
3740      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
3741      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
3742      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
3743      * is unknown.)
3744      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
3745      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
3746      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
3747      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
3748      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
3749      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
3750      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
3751      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
3752      * <p>
3753      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
3754      * @param type the desired target type
3755      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
3756      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
3757      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
3758      */
3759     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
3760         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
3761     }
3762 
3763     /**
3764      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
3765      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
3766      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
3767      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
3768      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
3769      * <p>
3770      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
3771      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
3772      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
3773      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
3774      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
3775      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
3776      * <p>
3777      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
3778      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
3779      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
3780      * <em>Discussion:</em>
3781      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
3782      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
3783      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
3784      * of the same arity as the general type.
3785      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
3786      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
3787      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
3788      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
3789      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
3790      * <p>
3791      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
3792      * @param type the desired target type
3793      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
3794      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
3795      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
3796      */
3797     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
3798         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
3799     }

3801     /**
3802      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to

3812      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is of the given type.

3822      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
3823      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
3824      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
3825      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
3826      * <p>
3827      * Before invoking its target, if the access mode type differs from the
3828      * desired given type, the invoker will apply reference casts as necessary
3829      * and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by
3830      * {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.  Similarly, the return value will be

3851 
3852      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
3853 
3854     /**
3855      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
3856      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
3857      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
3858      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
3859      * which is equal to the desired new type.
3860      * <p>
3861      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
3862      * <p>
3863      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
3864      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
3865      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
3866      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
3867      * <ul>
3868      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
3869      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
3870      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
3871      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
3872      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
3873      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
3874      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
3875      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
3876      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
3877      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
3878      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
3879      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
3880      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
3881      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
3882      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
3883      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
3884      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
3885      *     the low-order bit.
3886      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
3887      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
3888      * </ul>
3889      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
3890      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
3891      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
3892      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
3893      *           necessary return value conversions
3894      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
3895      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
3896      * @see MethodHandle#asType
3897      */
3898     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
3899         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
3900         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
3901         MethodType oldType = target.type();
3902         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
3903         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
3904             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
3905         }
3906         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
3907     }
3908 
3909     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
3910         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
3911             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
3912         }
3913     }
3914 
3915     /**
3916      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
3917      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
3918      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
3919      * which is equal to the desired new type.
3920      * <p>
3921      * The given array controls the reordering.
3922      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
3923      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
3924      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
3925      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
3926      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
3927      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
3928      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
3929      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
3930      * <p>
3931      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
3932      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
3933      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
3934      * or parameters in the target method handle.
3935      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
3936      * type of the original target.
3937      * <p>
3938      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
3939      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
3940      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
3941      * if its index does not appear in the array.
3942      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
3943      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
3944      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
3945      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
3946 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
3947 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
3948 ...
3949 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
3950 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
3951 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
3952 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
3953 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
3954 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
3955 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
3956 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
3957 assert(add.type().equals(intfn2));
3958 MethodHandle twice = permuteArguments(add, intfn1, 0, 0);
3959 assert(twice.type().equals(intfn1));
3960 assert((int)twice.invokeExact(21) == 42);
3961      * }</pre></blockquote>
3962      * <p>
3963      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
3964      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
3965      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are reordered
3966      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
3967      * @param reorder an index array which controls the reordering
3968      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after it
3969      *           drops unused arguments and moves and/or duplicates the other arguments
3970      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3971      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the index array length is not equal to
3972      *                  the arity of the target, or if any index array element
3973      *                  not a valid index for a parameter of {@code newType},
3974      *                  or if two corresponding parameter types in
3975      *                  {@code target.type()} and {@code newType} are not identical,
3976      */
3977     public static MethodHandle permuteArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType, int... reorder) {
3978         reorder = reorder.clone();  // get a private copy
3979         MethodType oldType = target.type();
3980         permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType);
3981         // first detect dropped arguments and handle them separately
3982         int[] originalReorder = reorder;
3983         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
3984         LambdaForm form = result.form;
3985         int newArity = newType.parameterCount();
3986         // Normalize the reordering into a real permutation,
3987         // by removing duplicates and adding dropped elements.
3988         // This somewhat improves lambda form caching, as well
3989         // as simplifying the transform by breaking it up into steps.
3990         for (int ddIdx; (ddIdx = findFirstDupOrDrop(reorder, newArity)) != 0; ) {
3991             if (ddIdx > 0) {
3992                 // We found a duplicated entry at reorder[ddIdx].
3993                 // Example:  (x,y,z)->asList(x,y,z)
3994                 // permuted by [1*,0,1] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a1,a0,a1)
3995                 // permuted by [0,1,0*] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a0,a1,a0)
3996                 // The starred element corresponds to the argument
3997                 // deleted by the dupArgumentForm transform.
3998                 int srcPos = ddIdx, dstPos = srcPos, dupVal = reorder[srcPos];
3999                 boolean killFirst = false;
4000                 for (int val; (val = reorder[--dstPos]) != dupVal; ) {
4001                     // Set killFirst if the dup is larger than an intervening position.
4002                     // This will remove at least one inversion from the permutation.
4003                     if (dupVal > val) killFirst = true;
4004                 }
4005                 if (!killFirst) {
4006                     srcPos = dstPos;
4007                     dstPos = ddIdx;
4008                 }
4009                 form = form.editor().dupArgumentForm(1 + srcPos, 1 + dstPos);
4010                 assert (reorder[srcPos] == reorder[dstPos]);
4011                 oldType = oldType.dropParameterTypes(dstPos, dstPos + 1);
4012                 // contract the reordering by removing the element at dstPos
4013                 int tailPos = dstPos + 1;
4014                 System.arraycopy(reorder, tailPos, reorder, dstPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4015                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length - 1);
4016             } else {
4017                 int dropVal = ~ddIdx, insPos = 0;
4018                 while (insPos < reorder.length && reorder[insPos] < dropVal) {
4019                     // Find first element of reorder larger than dropVal.
4020                     // This is where we will insert the dropVal.
4021                     insPos += 1;
4022                 }
4023                 Class<?> ptype = newType.parameterType(dropVal);
4024                 form = form.editor().addArgumentForm(1 + insPos, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4025                 oldType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(insPos, ptype);
4026                 // expand the reordering by inserting an element at insPos
4027                 int tailPos = insPos + 1;
4028                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length + 1);
4029                 System.arraycopy(reorder, insPos, reorder, tailPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4030                 reorder[insPos] = dropVal;
4031             }
4032             assert (permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType));
4033         }
4034         assert (reorder.length == newArity);  // a perfect permutation
4035         // Note:  This may cache too many distinct LFs. Consider backing off to varargs code.
4036         form = form.editor().permuteArgumentsForm(1, reorder);
4037         if (newType == result.type() && form == result.internalForm())
4038             return result;
4039         return result.copyWith(newType, form);
4040     }
4041 
4042     /**
4043      * Return an indication of any duplicate or omission in reorder.
4044      * If the reorder contains a duplicate entry, return the index of the second occurrence.
4045      * Otherwise, return ~(n), for the first n in [0..newArity-1] that is not present in reorder.
4046      * Otherwise, return zero.
4047      * If an element not in [0..newArity-1] is encountered, return reorder.length.
4048      */
4049     private static int findFirstDupOrDrop(int[] reorder, int newArity) {
4050         final int BIT_LIMIT = 63;  // max number of bits in bit mask
4051         if (newArity < BIT_LIMIT) {
4052             long mask = 0;
4053             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4054                 int arg = reorder[i];
4055                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4056                     return reorder.length;
4057                 }
4058                 long bit = 1L << arg;
4059                 if ((mask & bit) != 0) {
4060                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4061                 }
4062                 mask |= bit;
4063             }
4064             if (mask == (1L << newArity) - 1) {
4065                 assert(Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(Long.lowestOneBit(~mask)) == newArity);
4066                 return 0;
4067             }
4068             // find first zero
4069             long zeroBit = Long.lowestOneBit(~mask);
4070             int zeroPos = Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(zeroBit);
4071             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4072             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4073                 return 0;
4074             }
4075             return ~zeroPos;
4076         } else {
4077             // same algorithm, different bit set
4078             BitSet mask = new BitSet(newArity);
4079             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4080                 int arg = reorder[i];
4081                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4082                     return reorder.length;
4083                 }
4084                 if (mask.get(arg)) {
4085                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4086                 }
4087                 mask.set(arg);
4088             }
4089             int zeroPos = mask.nextClearBit(0);
4090             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4091             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4092                 return 0;
4093             }
4094             return ~zeroPos;
4095         }
4096     }
4097 
4098     private static boolean permuteArgumentChecks(int[] reorder, MethodType newType, MethodType oldType) {
4099         if (newType.returnType() != oldType.returnType())
4100             throw newIllegalArgumentException("return types do not match",
4101                     oldType, newType);
4102         if (reorder.length == oldType.parameterCount()) {
4103             int limit = newType.parameterCount();
4104             boolean bad = false;
4105             for (int j = 0; j < reorder.length; j++) {
4106                 int i = reorder[j];
4107                 if (i < 0 || i >= limit) {
4108                     bad = true; break;
4109                 }
4110                 Class<?> src = newType.parameterType(i);
4111                 Class<?> dst = oldType.parameterType(j);
4112                 if (src != dst)
4113                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("parameter types do not match after reorder",
4114                             oldType, newType);
4115             }
4116             if (!bad)  return true;
4117         }
4118         throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad reorder array: "+Arrays.toString(reorder));
4119     }
4120 
4121     /**
4122      * Produces a method handle of the requested return type which returns the given
4123      * constant value every time it is invoked.
4124      * <p>
4125      * Before the method handle is returned, the passed-in value is converted to the requested type.
4126      * If the requested type is primitive, widening primitive conversions are attempted,
4127      * else reference conversions are attempted.
4128      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code identity(type).bindTo(value)}.
4129      * @param type the return type of the desired method handle
4130      * @param value the value to return
4131      * @return a method handle of the given return type and no arguments, which always returns the given value
4132      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code type} argument is null
4133      * @throws ClassCastException if the value cannot be converted to the required return type
4134      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4135      */
4136     public static MethodHandle constant(Class<?> type, Object value) {
4137         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4138             if (type == void.class)
4139                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("void type");
4140             Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type);
4141             value = w.convert(value, type);
4142             if (w.zero().equals(value))
4143                 return zero(w, type);
4144             return insertArguments(identity(type), 0, value);
4145         } else {
4146             if (value == null)
4147                 return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4148             return identity(type).bindTo(value);
4149         }
4150     }
4151 
4152     /**
4153      * Produces a method handle which returns its sole argument when invoked.
4154      * @param type the type of the sole parameter and return value of the desired method handle
4155      * @return a unary method handle which accepts and returns the given type
4156      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4157      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4158      */
4159     public static MethodHandle identity(Class<?> type) {
4160         Wrapper btw = (type.isPrimitive() ? Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type) : Wrapper.OBJECT);
4161         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4162         MethodHandle ident = IDENTITY_MHS[pos];
4163         if (ident == null) {
4164             ident = setCachedMethodHandle(IDENTITY_MHS, pos, makeIdentity(btw.primitiveType()));
4165         }
4166         if (ident.type().returnType() == type)
4167             return ident;
4168         // something like identity(Foo.class); do not bother to intern these
4169         assert (btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4170         return makeIdentity(type);
4171     }
4172 
4173     /**
4174      * Produces a constant method handle of the requested return type which
4175      * returns the default value for that type every time it is invoked.
4176      * The resulting constant method handle will have no side effects.
4177      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code empty(methodType(type))}.
4178      * It is also equivalent to {@code explicitCastArguments(constant(Object.class, null), methodType(type))},
4179      * since {@code explicitCastArguments} converts {@code null} to default values.
4180      * @param type the expected return type of the desired method handle
4181      * @return a constant method handle that takes no arguments
4182      *         and returns the default value of the given type (or void, if the type is void)
4183      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4184      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4185      * @see MethodHandles#empty
4186      * @see MethodHandles#explicitCastArguments
4187      * @since 9
4188      */
4189     public static MethodHandle zero(Class<?> type) {
4190         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4191         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4192             return zero(Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type), type);
4193         } else if (type.isInlineClass()) {
4194             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
4195         } else {
4196             return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4197         }
4198     }
4199 
4200     private static MethodHandle identityOrVoid(Class<?> type) {
4201         return type == void.class ? zero(type) : identity(type);
4202     }
4203 
4204     /**
4205      * Produces a method handle of the requested type which ignores any arguments, does nothing,
4206      * and returns a suitable default depending on the return type.
4207      * That is, it returns a zero primitive value, a {@code null}, or {@code void}.
4208      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to
4209      * {@code dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList())}.
4210      *
4211      * @apiNote Given a predicate and target, a useful "if-then" construct can be produced as
4212      * {@code guardWithTest(pred, target, empty(target.type())}.
4213      * @param type the type of the desired method handle
4214      * @return a constant method handle of the given type, which returns a default value of the given return type
4215      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4216      * @see MethodHandles#zero
4217      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4218      * @since 9
4219      */
4220     public static  MethodHandle empty(MethodType type) {
4221         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4222         return dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList());
4223     }
4224 
4225     private static final MethodHandle[] IDENTITY_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4226     private static MethodHandle makeIdentity(Class<?> ptype) {
4227         MethodType mtype = MethodType.methodType(ptype, ptype);
4228         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.identityForm(BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4229         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.IDENTITY);
4230     }
4231 
4232     private static MethodHandle zero(Wrapper btw, Class<?> rtype) {
4233         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4234         MethodHandle zero = ZERO_MHS[pos];
4235         if (zero == null) {
4236             zero = setCachedMethodHandle(ZERO_MHS, pos, makeZero(btw.primitiveType()));
4237         }
4238         if (zero.type().returnType() == rtype)
4239             return zero;
4240         assert(btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4241         return makeZero(rtype);
4242     }
4243     private static final MethodHandle[] ZERO_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4244     private static MethodHandle makeZero(Class<?> rtype) {
4245         MethodType mtype = methodType(rtype);
4246         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.zeroForm(BasicType.basicType(rtype));
4247         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.ZERO);
4248     }
4249 
4250     private static synchronized MethodHandle setCachedMethodHandle(MethodHandle[] cache, int pos, MethodHandle value) {
4251         // Simulate a CAS, to avoid racy duplication of results.
4252         MethodHandle prev = cache[pos];
4253         if (prev != null) return prev;
4254         return cache[pos] = value;
4255     }
4256 
4257     /**
4258      * Provides a target method handle with one or more <em>bound arguments</em>
4259      * in advance of the method handle's invocation.
4260      * The formal parameters to the target corresponding to the bound
4261      * arguments are called <em>bound parameters</em>.
4262      * Returns a new method handle which saves away the bound arguments.
4263      * When it is invoked, it receives arguments for any non-bound parameters,
4264      * binds the saved arguments to their corresponding parameters,
4265      * and calls the original target.
4266      * <p>
4267      * The type of the new method handle will drop the types for the bound
4268      * parameters from the original target type, since the new method handle
4269      * will no longer require those arguments to be supplied by its callers.
4270      * <p>
4271      * Each given argument object must match the corresponding bound parameter type.
4272      * If a bound parameter type is a primitive, the argument object
4273      * must be a wrapper, and will be unboxed to produce the primitive value.
4274      * <p>
4275      * The {@code pos} argument selects which parameters are to be bound.
4276      * It may range between zero and <i>N-L</i> (inclusively),
4277      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target method handle
4278      * and <i>L</i> is the length of the values array.
4279      * <p>
4280      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4281      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4282      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the argument is inserted
4283      * @param pos where to insert the argument (zero for the first)
4284      * @param values the series of arguments to insert
4285      * @return a method handle which inserts an additional argument,
4286      *         before calling the original method handle
4287      * @throws NullPointerException if the target or the {@code values} array is null
4288      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if (@code pos) is less than {@code 0} or greater than
4289      *         {@code N - L} where {@code N} is the arity of the target method handle and {@code L}
4290      *         is the length of the values array.
4291      * @throws ClassCastException if an argument does not match the corresponding bound parameter
4292      *         type.
4293      * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
4294      */
4295     public static MethodHandle insertArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Object... values) {
4296         int insCount = values.length;
4297         Class<?>[] ptypes = insertArgumentsChecks(target, insCount, pos);
4298         if (insCount == 0)  return target;
4299         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4300         for (int i = 0; i < insCount; i++) {
4301             Object value = values[i];
4302             Class<?> ptype = ptypes[pos+i];
4303             if (ptype.isPrimitive()) {
4304                 result = insertArgumentPrimitive(result, pos, ptype, value);
4305             } else {
4306                 value = ptype.cast(value);  // throw CCE if needed
4307                 result = result.bindArgumentL(pos, value);
4308             }
4309         }
4310         return result;
4311     }
4312 
4313     private static BoundMethodHandle insertArgumentPrimitive(BoundMethodHandle result, int pos,
4314                                                              Class<?> ptype, Object value) {
4315         Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(ptype);
4316         // perform unboxing and/or primitive conversion
4317         value = w.convert(value, ptype);
4318         switch (w) {
4319         case INT:     return result.bindArgumentI(pos, (int)value);
4320         case LONG:    return result.bindArgumentJ(pos, (long)value);
4321         case FLOAT:   return result.bindArgumentF(pos, (float)value);
4322         case DOUBLE:  return result.bindArgumentD(pos, (double)value);
4323         default:      return result.bindArgumentI(pos, ValueConversions.widenSubword(value));
4324         }
4325     }
4326 
4327     private static Class<?>[] insertArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int insCount, int pos) throws RuntimeException {
4328         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4329         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4330         int inargs  = outargs - insCount;
4331         if (inargs < 0)
4332             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many values to insert");
4333         if (pos < 0 || pos > inargs)
4334             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to append");
4335         return oldType.ptypes();
4336     }
4337 
4338     /**
4339      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4340      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4341      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4342      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4343      * at some given position.
4344      * <p>
4345      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4346      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4347      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4348      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4349      * they will come after.
4350      * <p>
4351      * <b>Example:</b>
4352      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4353 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4354 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4355 ...
4356 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4357   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4358 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4359 MethodType bigType = cat.type().insertParameterTypes(0, int.class, String.class);
4360 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, bigType.parameterList().subList(0,2));
4361 assertEquals(bigType, d0.type());
4362 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact(123, "x", "y", "z"));
4363      * }</pre></blockquote>
4364      * <p>
4365      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
4366      * <blockquote><pre>
4367      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,Class...) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, valueTypes.toArray(new Class[0]))}
4368      * </pre></blockquote>
4369      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
4370      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
4371      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
4372      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
4373      *         before calling the original method handle
4374      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
4375      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} list or any of its elements is null
4376      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
4377      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4378      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have too many parameters
4379      */
4380     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4381         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes.toArray()));
4382     }
4383 
4384     private static List<Class<?>> copyTypes(Object[] array) {
4385         return Arrays.asList(Arrays.copyOf(array, array.length, Class[].class));
4386     }
4387 
4388     private static MethodHandle dropArguments0(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4389         MethodType oldType = target.type();  // get NPE
4390         int dropped = dropArgumentChecks(oldType, pos, valueTypes);
4391         MethodType newType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(pos, valueTypes);
4392         if (dropped == 0)  return target;
4393         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4394         LambdaForm lform = result.form;
4395         int insertFormArg = 1 + pos;
4396         for (Class<?> ptype : valueTypes) {
4397             lform = lform.editor().addArgumentForm(insertFormArg++, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4398         }
4399         result = result.copyWith(newType, lform);
4400         return result;
4401     }
4402 
4403     private static int dropArgumentChecks(MethodType oldType, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4404         int dropped = valueTypes.size();
4405         MethodType.checkSlotCount(dropped);
4406         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4407         int inargs  = outargs + dropped;
4408         if (pos < 0 || pos > outargs)
4409             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to remove"
4410                     + Arrays.asList(oldType, pos, valueTypes, inargs, outargs)
4411                     );
4412         return dropped;
4413     }
4414 
4415     /**
4416      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4417      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4418      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4419      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4420      * at some given position.
4421      * <p>
4422      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4423      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4424      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4425      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4426      * they will come after.
4427      * @apiNote
4428      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4429 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4430 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4431 ...
4432 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4433   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4434 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4435 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, String.class);
4436 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4437 MethodHandle d1 = dropArguments(cat, 1, String.class);
4438 assertEquals("xz", (String) d1.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4439 MethodHandle d2 = dropArguments(cat, 2, String.class);
4440 assertEquals("xy", (String) d2.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4441 MethodHandle d12 = dropArguments(cat, 1, int.class, boolean.class);
4442 assertEquals("xz", (String) d12.invokeExact("x", 12, true, "z"));
4443      * }</pre></blockquote>
4444      * <p>
4445      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
4446      * <blockquote><pre>
4447      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, Arrays.asList(valueTypes))}
4448      * </pre></blockquote>
4449      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
4450      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
4451      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
4452      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
4453      *         before calling the original method handle
4454      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
4455      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} array or any of its elements is null
4456      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
4457      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4458      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have
4459      *                  <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4460      */
4461     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Class<?>... valueTypes) {
4462         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes));
4463     }
4464 
4465     // private version which allows caller some freedom with error handling
4466     private static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos,
4467                                       boolean nullOnFailure) {
4468         newTypes = copyTypes(newTypes.toArray());
4469         List<Class<?>> oldTypes = target.type().parameterList();
4470         int match = oldTypes.size();
4471         if (skip != 0) {
4472             if (skip < 0 || skip > match) {
4473                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal skip", skip, target);
4474             }
4475             oldTypes = oldTypes.subList(skip, match);
4476             match -= skip;
4477         }
4478         List<Class<?>> addTypes = newTypes;
4479         int add = addTypes.size();
4480         if (pos != 0) {
4481             if (pos < 0 || pos > add) {
4482                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal pos", pos, newTypes);
4483             }
4484             addTypes = addTypes.subList(pos, add);
4485             add -= pos;
4486             assert(addTypes.size() == add);
4487         }
4488         // Do not add types which already match the existing arguments.
4489         if (match > add || !oldTypes.equals(addTypes.subList(0, match))) {
4490             if (nullOnFailure) {
4491                 return null;
4492             }
4493             throw newIllegalArgumentException("argument lists do not match", oldTypes, newTypes);
4494         }
4495         addTypes = addTypes.subList(match, add);
4496         add -= match;
4497         assert(addTypes.size() == add);
4498         // newTypes:     (   P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
4499         // target: ( S*[skip],        M*[match]  )
4500         MethodHandle adapter = target;
4501         if (add > 0) {
4502             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip+ match, addTypes);
4503         }
4504         // adapter: (S*[skip],        M*[match], A*[add] )
4505         if (pos > 0) {
4506             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip, newTypes.subList(0, pos));
4507         }
4508         // adapter: (S*[skip], P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
4509         return adapter;
4510     }
4511 
4512     /**
4513      * Adapts a target method handle to match the given parameter type list. If necessary, adds dummy arguments. Some
4514      * leading parameters can be skipped before matching begins. The remaining types in the {@code target}'s parameter
4515      * type list must be a sub-list of the {@code newTypes} type list at the starting position {@code pos}. The
4516      * resulting handle will have the target handle's parameter type list, with any non-matching parameter types (before
4517      * or after the matching sub-list) inserted in corresponding positions of the target's original parameters, as if by
4518      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
4519      * <p>
4520      * The resulting handle will have the same return type as the target handle.
4521      * <p>
4522      * In more formal terms, assume these two type lists:<ul>
4523      * <li>The target handle has the parameter type list {@code S..., M...}, with as many types in {@code S} as
4524      * indicated by {@code skip}. The {@code M} types are those that are supposed to match part of the given type list,
4525      * {@code newTypes}.
4526      * <li>The {@code newTypes} list contains types {@code P..., M..., A...}, with as many types in {@code P} as
4527      * indicated by {@code pos}. The {@code M} types are precisely those that the {@code M} types in the target handle's
4528      * parameter type list are supposed to match. The types in {@code A} are additional types found after the matching
4529      * sub-list.
4530      * </ul>
4531      * Given these assumptions, the result of an invocation of {@code dropArgumentsToMatch} will have the parameter type
4532      * list {@code S..., P..., M..., A...}, with the {@code P} and {@code A} types inserted as if by
4533      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
4534      *
4535      * @apiNote
4536      * Two method handles whose argument lists are "effectively identical" (i.e., identical in a common prefix) may be
4537      * mutually converted to a common type by two calls to {@code dropArgumentsToMatch}, as follows:
4538      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4539 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4540 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4541 ...
4542 ...
4543 MethodHandle h0 = constant(boolean.class, true);
4544 MethodHandle h1 = lookup().findVirtual(String.class, "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4545 MethodType bigType = h1.type().insertParameterTypes(1, String.class, int.class);
4546 MethodHandle h2 = dropArguments(h1, 0, bigType.parameterList());
4547 if (h1.type().parameterCount() < h2.type().parameterCount())
4548     h1 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h1, 0, h2.type().parameterList(), 0);  // lengthen h1
4549 else
4550     h2 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h2, 0, h1.type().parameterList(), 0);    // lengthen h2
4551 MethodHandle h3 = guardWithTest(h0, h1, h2);
4552 assertEquals("xy", h3.invoke("x", "y", 1, "a", "b", "c"));
4553      * }</pre></blockquote>
4554      * @param target the method handle to adapt
4555      * @param skip number of targets parameters to disregard (they will be unchanged)
4556      * @param newTypes the list of types to match {@code target}'s parameter type list to
4557      * @param pos place in {@code newTypes} where the non-skipped target parameters must occur
4558      * @return a possibly adapted method handle
4559      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4560      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code newTypes} is {@code void.class},
4561      *         or if {@code skip} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4562      *         or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the newTypes list size,
4563      *         or if {@code newTypes} does not contain the {@code target}'s non-skipped parameter types at position
4564      *         {@code pos}.
4565      * @since 9
4566      */
4567     public static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos) {
4568         Objects.requireNonNull(target);
4569         Objects.requireNonNull(newTypes);
4570         return dropArgumentsToMatch(target, skip, newTypes, pos, false);
4571     }
4572 
4573     /**
4574      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
4575      * one or more of its arguments, each with its own unary filter function,
4576      * and then calling the target with each pre-processed argument
4577      * replaced by the result of its corresponding filter function.
4578      * <p>
4579      * The pre-processing is performed by one or more method handles,
4580      * specified in the elements of the {@code filters} array.
4581      * The first element of the filter array corresponds to the {@code pos}
4582      * argument of the target, and so on in sequence.
4583      * The filter functions are invoked in left to right order.
4584      * <p>
4585      * Null arguments in the array are treated as identity functions,
4586      * and the corresponding arguments left unchanged.
4587      * (If there are no non-null elements in the array, the original target is returned.)
4588      * Each filter is applied to the corresponding argument of the adapter.
4589      * <p>
4590      * If a filter {@code F} applies to the {@code N}th argument of
4591      * the target, then {@code F} must be a method handle which
4592      * takes exactly one argument.  The type of {@code F}'s sole argument
4593      * replaces the corresponding argument type of the target
4594      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
4595      * The return type of {@code F} must be identical to the corresponding
4596      * parameter type of the target.
4597      * <p>
4598      * It is an error if there are elements of {@code filters}
4599      * (null or not)
4600      * which do not correspond to argument positions in the target.
4601      * <p><b>Example:</b>
4602      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4603 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4604 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4605 ...
4606 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4607   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4608 MethodHandle upcase = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4609   "toUpperCase", methodType(String.class));
4610 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4611 MethodHandle f0 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase);
4612 assertEquals("Xy", (String) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // Xy
4613 MethodHandle f1 = filterArguments(cat, 1, upcase);
4614 assertEquals("xY", (String) f1.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xY
4615 MethodHandle f2 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase, upcase);
4616 assertEquals("XY", (String) f2.invokeExact("x", "y")); // XY
4617      * }</pre></blockquote>
4618      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
4619      * denotes the return type of both the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
4620      * {@code P}/{@code p} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values
4621      * of the parameters and arguments that precede and follow the filter position
4622      * {@code pos}, respectively. {@code A[i]}/{@code a[i]} stand for the types and
4623      * values of the filtered parameters and arguments; they also represent the
4624      * return types of the {@code filter[i]} handles. The latter accept arguments
4625      * {@code v[i]} of type {@code V[i]}, which also appear in the signature of
4626      * the resulting adapter.
4627      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4628      * T target(P... p, A[i]... a[i], B... b);
4629      * A[i] filter[i](V[i]);
4630      * T adapter(P... p, V[i]... v[i], B... b) {
4631      *   return target(p..., filter[i](v[i])..., b...);
4632      * }
4633      * }</pre></blockquote>
4634      * <p>
4635      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4636      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4637      *
4638      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are filtered
4639      * @param pos the position of the first argument to filter
4640      * @param filters method handles to call initially on filtered arguments
4641      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument filtering logic
4642      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null
4643      *                              or if the {@code filters} array is null
4644      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if a non-null element of {@code filters}
4645      *          does not match a corresponding argument type of target as described above,
4646      *          or if the {@code pos+filters.length} is greater than {@code target.type().parameterCount()},
4647      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4648      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4649      */
4650     public static MethodHandle filterArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle... filters) {
4651         // In method types arguments start at index 0, while the LF
4652         // editor have the MH receiver at position 0 - adjust appropriately.
4653         final int MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET = 1;
4654         filterArgumentsCheckArity(target, pos, filters);
4655         MethodHandle adapter = target;
4656 
4657         // keep track of currently matched filters, as to optimize repeated filters
4658         int index = 0;
4659         int[] positions = new int[filters.length];
4660         MethodHandle filter = null;
4661 
4662         // process filters in reverse order so that the invocation of
4663         // the resulting adapter will invoke the filters in left-to-right order
4664         for (int i = filters.length - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
4665             MethodHandle newFilter = filters[i];
4666             if (newFilter == null) continue;  // ignore null elements of filters
4667 
4668             // flush changes on update
4669             if (filter != newFilter) {
4670                 if (filter != null) {
4671                     if (index > 1) {
4672                         adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
4673                     } else {
4674                         adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
4675                     }
4676                 }
4677                 filter = newFilter;
4678                 index = 0;
4679             }
4680 
4681             filterArgumentChecks(target, pos + i, newFilter);
4682             positions[index++] = pos + i + MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET;
4683         }
4684         if (index > 1) {
4685             adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
4686         } else if (index == 1) {
4687             adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
4688         }
4689         return adapter;
4690     }
4691 
4692     private static MethodHandle filterRepeatedArgument(MethodHandle adapter, MethodHandle filter, int[] positions) {
4693         MethodType targetType = adapter.type();
4694         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4695         BoundMethodHandle result = adapter.rebind();
4696         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
4697 
4698         Class<?>[] ptypes = targetType.ptypes().clone();
4699         for (int pos : positions) {
4700             ptypes[pos - 1] = newParamType;
4701         }
4702         MethodType newType = MethodType.makeImpl(targetType.rtype(), ptypes, true);
4703 
4704         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterRepeatedArgumentForm(BasicType.basicType(newParamType), positions);
4705         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
4706     }
4707 
4708     /*non-public*/
4709     static MethodHandle filterArgument(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
4710         filterArgumentChecks(target, pos, filter);
4711         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4712         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4713         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4714         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
4715         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterArgumentForm(1 + pos, BasicType.basicType(newParamType));
4716         MethodType newType = targetType.changeParameterType(pos, newParamType);
4717         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
4718         return result;
4719     }
4720 
4721     private static void filterArgumentsCheckArity(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle[] filters) {
4722         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4723         int maxPos = targetType.parameterCount();
4724         if (pos + filters.length > maxPos)
4725             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many filters");
4726     }
4727 
4728     private static void filterArgumentChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
4729         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4730         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4731         if (filterType.parameterCount() != 1
4732             || filterType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(pos))
4733             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
4734     }
4735 
4736     /**
4737      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
4738      * a sub-sequence of its arguments with a filter (another method handle).
4739      * The pre-processed arguments are replaced by the result (if any) of the
4740      * filter function.
4741      * The target is then called on the modified (usually shortened) argument list.
4742      * <p>
4743      * If the filter returns a value, the target must accept that value as
4744      * its argument in position {@code pos}, preceded and/or followed by
4745      * any arguments not passed to the filter.
4746      * If the filter returns void, the target must accept all arguments
4747      * not passed to the filter.
4748      * No arguments are reordered, and a result returned from the filter
4749      * replaces (in order) the whole subsequence of arguments originally
4750      * passed to the adapter.
4751      * <p>
4752      * The argument types (if any) of the filter
4753      * replace zero or one argument types of the target, at position {@code pos},
4754      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
4755      * The return type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
4756      * argument type of the target at position {@code pos}, and that target argument
4757      * is supplied by the return value of the filter.
4758      * <p>
4759      * In all cases, {@code pos} must be greater than or equal to zero, and
4760      * {@code pos} must also be less than or equal to the target's arity.
4761      * <p><b>Example:</b>
4762      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4763 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4764 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4765 ...
4766 MethodHandle deepToString = publicLookup()
4767   .findStatic(Arrays.class, "deepToString", methodType(String.class, Object[].class));
4768 
4769 MethodHandle ts1 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 1);
4770 assertEquals("[strange]", (String) ts1.invokeExact("strange"));
4771 
4772 MethodHandle ts2 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 2);
4773 assertEquals("[up, down]", (String) ts2.invokeExact("up", "down"));
4774 
4775 MethodHandle ts3 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 3);
4776 MethodHandle ts3_ts2 = collectArguments(ts3, 1, ts2);
4777 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], strange]",
4778              (String) ts3_ts2.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
4779 
4780 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts1 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 3, ts1);
4781 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], [strange]]",
4782              (String) ts3_ts2_ts1.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
4783 
4784 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts3 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 1, ts3);
4785 assertEquals("[top, [[up, down, strange], charm], bottom]",
4786              (String) ts3_ts2_ts3.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange", "charm", "bottom"));
4787      * }</pre></blockquote>
4788      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
4789      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
4790      * {@code V}/{@code v} stand for the return type and value of the
4791      * {@code filter}, which are also found in the signature and arguments of
4792      * the {@code target}, respectively, unless {@code V} is {@code void}.
4793      * {@code A}/{@code a} and {@code C}/{@code c} represent the parameter types
4794      * and values preceding and following the collection position, {@code pos},
4795      * in the {@code target}'s signature. They also turn up in the resulting
4796      * adapter's signature and arguments, where they surround
4797      * {@code B}/{@code b}, which represent the parameter types and arguments
4798      * to the {@code filter} (if any).
4799      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4800      * T target(A...,V,C...);
4801      * V filter(B...);
4802      * T adapter(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
4803      *   V v = filter(b...);
4804      *   return target(a...,v,c...);
4805      * }
4806      * // and if the filter has no arguments:
4807      * T target2(A...,V,C...);
4808      * V filter2();
4809      * T adapter2(A... a,C... c) {
4810      *   V v = filter2();
4811      *   return target2(a...,v,c...);
4812      * }
4813      * // and if the filter has a void return:
4814      * T target3(A...,C...);
4815      * void filter3(B...);
4816      * T adapter3(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
4817      *   filter3(b...);
4818      *   return target3(a...,c...);
4819      * }
4820      * }</pre></blockquote>
4821      * <p>
4822      * A collection adapter {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)} is equivalent to
4823      * one which first "folds" the affected arguments, and then drops them, in separate
4824      * steps as follows:
4825      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4826      * mh = MethodHandles.dropArguments(mh, 1, coll.type().parameterList()); //step 2
4827      * mh = MethodHandles.foldArguments(mh, coll); //step 1
4828      * }</pre></blockquote>
