4829      * If the target method handle consumes no arguments besides than the result
4830      * (if any) of the filter {@code coll}, then {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)}
4831      * is equivalent to {@code filterReturnValue(coll, mh)}.
4832      * If the filter method handle {@code coll} consumes one argument and produces
4833      * a non-void result, then {@code collectArguments(mh, N, coll)}
4834      * is equivalent to {@code filterArguments(mh, N, coll)}.
4835      * Other equivalences are possible but would require argument permutation.
4836      * <p>
4837      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4838      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4839      *
4840      * @param target the method handle to invoke after filtering the subsequence of arguments
4841      * @param pos the position of the first adapter argument to pass to the filter,
4842      *            and/or the target argument which receives the result of the filter
4843      * @param filter method handle to call on the subsequence of arguments
4844      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument subsequence filtering logic
4845      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4846      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the return type of {@code filter}
4847      *          is non-void and is not the same as the {@code pos} argument of the target,
4848      *          or if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target's arity, inclusive,
4849      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4850      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4851      * @see MethodHandles#foldArguments
4852      * @see MethodHandles#filterArguments
4853      * @see MethodHandles#filterReturnValue
4854      */
4855     public static MethodHandle collectArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
4856         MethodType newType = collectArgumentsChecks(target, pos, filter);
4857         MethodType collectorType = filter.type();
4858         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4859         LambdaForm lform;
4860         if (collectorType.returnType().isArray() && filter.intrinsicName() == Intrinsic.NEW_ARRAY) {
4861             lform = result.editor().collectArgumentArrayForm(1 + pos, filter);
4862             if (lform != null) {
4863                 return result.copyWith(newType, lform);
4864             }
4865         }
4866         lform = result.editor().collectArgumentsForm(1 + pos, collectorType.basicType());
4867         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
4868     }
4869 
4870     private static MethodType collectArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
4871         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4872         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4873         Class<?> rtype = filterType.returnType();
4874         List<Class<?>> filterArgs = filterType.parameterList();
4875         if (rtype == void.class) {
4876             return targetType.insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
4877         }
4878         if (rtype != targetType.parameterType(pos)) {
4879             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
4880         }
4881         return targetType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos+1).insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
4882     }
4883 
4884     /**
4885      * Adapts a target method handle by post-processing
4886      * its return value (if any) with a filter (another method handle).
4887      * The result of the filter is returned from the adapter.
4888      * <p>
4889      * If the target returns a value, the filter must accept that value as
4890      * its only argument.
4891      * If the target returns void, the filter must accept no arguments.
4892      * <p>
4893      * The return type of the filter
4894      * replaces the return type of the target
4895      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
4896      * The argument type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
4897      * return type of the target.
4898      * <p><b>Example:</b>
4899      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4900 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4901 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4902 ...
4903 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4904   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4905 MethodHandle length = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4906   "length", methodType(int.class));
4907 System.out.println((String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xy
4908 MethodHandle f0 = filterReturnValue(cat, length);
4909 System.out.println((int) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // 2
4910      * }</pre></blockquote>
4911      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code,
4912      * {@code T}/{@code t} represent the result type and value of the
4913      * {@code target}; {@code V}, the result type of the {@code filter}; and
4914      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the parameters and arguments
4915      * of the {@code target} as well as the resulting adapter.
4916      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4917      * T target(A...);
4918      * V filter(T);
4919      * V adapter(A... a) {
4920      *   T t = target(a...);
4921      *   return filter(t);
4922      * }
4923      * // and if the target has a void return:
4924      * void target2(A...);
4925      * V filter2();
4926      * V adapter2(A... a) {
4927      *   target2(a...);
4928      *   return filter2();
4929      * }
4930      * // and if the filter has a void return:
4931      * T target3(A...);
4932      * void filter3(V);
4933      * void adapter3(A... a) {
4934      *   T t = target3(a...);
4935      *   filter3(t);
4936      * }
4937      * }</pre></blockquote>
4938      * <p>
4939      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4940      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4941      * @param target the method handle to invoke before filtering the return value
4942      * @param filter method handle to call on the return value
4943      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified return value filtering logic
4944      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4945      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the argument list of {@code filter}
4946      *          does not match the return type of target as described above
4947      */
4948     public static MethodHandle filterReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
4949         MethodType targetType = target.type();
4950         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
4951         filterReturnValueChecks(targetType, filterType);
4952         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4953         BasicType rtype = BasicType.basicType(filterType.returnType());
4954         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterReturnForm(rtype, false);
4955         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
4956         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
4957         return result;
4958     }
4959 
4960     private static void filterReturnValueChecks(MethodType targetType, MethodType filterType) throws RuntimeException {
4961         Class<?> rtype = targetType.returnType();
4962         int filterValues = filterType.parameterCount();
4963         if (filterValues == 0
4964                 ? (rtype != void.class)
4965                 : (rtype != filterType.parameterType(0) || filterValues != 1))
4966             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
4967     }
4968 
4969     /**
4970      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
4971      * some of its arguments, and then calling the target with
4972      * the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original
4973      * sequence of arguments.
4974      * <p>
4975      * The pre-processing is performed by {@code combiner}, a second method handle.
4976      * Of the arguments passed to the adapter, the first {@code N} arguments
4977      * are copied to the combiner, which is then called.
4978      * (Here, {@code N} is defined as the parameter count of the combiner.)
4979      * After this, control passes to the target, with any result
4980      * from the combiner inserted before the original {@code N} incoming
4981      * arguments.
4982      * <p>
4983      * If the combiner returns a value, the first parameter type of the target
4984      * must be identical with the return type of the combiner, and the next
4985      * {@code N} parameter types of the target must exactly match the parameters
4986      * of the combiner.
4987      * <p>
4988      * If the combiner has a void return, no result will be inserted,
4989      * and the first {@code N} parameter types of the target
4990      * must exactly match the parameters of the combiner.
4991      * <p>
4992      * The resulting adapter is the same type as the target, except that the
4993      * first parameter type is dropped,
4994      * if it corresponds to the result of the combiner.
4995      * <p>
4996      * (Note that {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments} can be used to remove any arguments
4997      * that either the combiner or the target does not wish to receive.
4998      * If some of the incoming arguments are destined only for the combiner,
4999      * consider using {@link MethodHandle#asCollector asCollector} instead, since those
5000      * arguments will not need to be live on the stack on entry to the
5001      * target.)
5002      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5003      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5004 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5005 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5006 ...
5007 MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5008   "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5009     .bindTo(System.out);
5010 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5011   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5012 assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5013 MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, trace);
5014 // also prints "boo":
5015 assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5016      * }</pre></blockquote>
5017      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5018      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5019      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5020      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5021      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5022      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5023      * position. {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values of the
5024      * {@code target} parameters and arguments that follow the folded parameters
5025      * and arguments.
5026      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5027      * // there are N arguments in A...
5028      * T target(V, A[N]..., B...);
5029      * V combiner(A...);
5030      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5031      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5032      *   return target(v, a..., b...);
5033      * }
5034      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5035      * T target2(A[N]..., B...);
5036      * void combiner2(A...);
5037      * T adapter2(A... a, B... b) {
5038      *   combiner2(a...);
5039      *   return target2(a..., b...);
5040      * }
5041      * }</pre></blockquote>
5042      * <p>
5043      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5044      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5045      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5046      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5047      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5048      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5049      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code combiner}'s return type
5050      *          is non-void and not the same as the first argument type of
5051      *          the target, or if the initial {@code N} argument types
5052      *          of the target
5053      *          (skipping one matching the {@code combiner}'s return type)
5054      *          are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}
5055      */
5056     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle combiner) {
5057         return foldArguments(target, 0, combiner);
5058     }
5059 
5060     /**
5061      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, starting at a given position, and then
5062      * calling the target with the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original sequence of arguments just
5063      * before the folded arguments.
5064      * <p>
5065      * This method is closely related to {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}, but allows to control the
5066      * position in the parameter list at which folding takes place. The argument controlling this, {@code pos}, is a
5067      * zero-based index. The aforementioned method {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)} assumes position
5068      * 0.
5069      *
5070      * @apiNote Example:
5071      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5072     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5073     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5074     ...
5075     MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5076     "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5077     .bindTo(System.out);
5078     MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5079     "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5080     assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5081     MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, 1, trace);
5082     // also prints "jum":
5083     assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5084      * }</pre></blockquote>
5085      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5086      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5087      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5088      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5089      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5090      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5091      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5092      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5093      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5094      * respectively.
5095      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5096      * // there are N arguments in A...
5097      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5098      * V combiner(A...);
5099      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5100      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5101      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5102      * }
5103      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5104      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5105      * void combiner2(A...);
5106      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5107      *   combiner2(a...);
5108      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5109      * }
5110      * }</pre></blockquote>
5111      * <p>
5112      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5113      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5114      *
5115      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5116      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5117      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5118      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5119      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5120      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5121      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5122      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5123      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5124      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5125      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5126      *
5127      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5128      * @since 9
5129      */
5130     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5131         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5132         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5133         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5134         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5135         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5136         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5137         MethodType newType = targetType;
5138         if (!dropResult) {
5139             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5140         }
5141         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5142         return result;
5143     }
5144 
5145     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5146         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5147         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5148         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5149         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5150         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5151         if (ok) {
5152             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5153                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5154                     ok = false;
5155                     break;
5156                 }
5157             }
5158         }
5159         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5160             ok = false;
5161         if (!ok)
5162             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5163         return rtype;
5164     }
5165 
5166     /**
5167      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5168      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5169      *
5170      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5171      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5172      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5173      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5174      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5175      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5176      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5177      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5178      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5179      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5180      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5181      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5182      */
5183     /*non-public*/
5184     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5185         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5186     }
5187 
5188     /**
5189      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5190      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5191      *
5192      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5193      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5194      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5195      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5196      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5197      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5198      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5199      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5200      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5201      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5202      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5203      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5204      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5205      */
5206     /*non-public*/
5207     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5208         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5209     }
5210 
5211     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5212         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5213         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5214         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5215         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5216 
5217         MethodType newType = targetType;
5218         LambdaForm lform;
5219         if (filter) {
5220             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5221         } else {
5222             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5223             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5224             if (!dropResult) {
5225                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5226             }
5227         }
5228         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5229         return result;
5230     }
5231 
5232     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5233         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5234         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5235             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5236         }
5237         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5238 
5239         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5240             int arg = argPos[i];
5241             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5242                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5243             }
5244             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5245                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5246                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5247                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5248             }
5249         }
5250         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5251             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5252         }
5253         return rtype;
5254     }
5255 
5256     /**
5257      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5258      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5259      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5260      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5261      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5262      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5263      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5264      * <p>
5265      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5266      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5267      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5268      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5269      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5270      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5271      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5272      * boolean test(A...);
5273      * T target(A...,B...);
5274      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5275      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5276      *   if (test(a...))
5277      *     return target(a..., b...);
5278      *   else
5279      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5280      * }
5281      * }</pre></blockquote>
5282      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5283      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5284      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5285      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5286      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5287      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5288      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5289      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5290      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5291      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5292      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5293      */
5294     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5295                                MethodHandle target,
5296                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5297         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5298         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5299         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5300         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
5301             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5302         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5303             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5304         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5305         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5306         if (test == null) {
5307             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5308         }
5309         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5310     }
5311 
5312     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5313         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5314     }
5315 
5316     /**
5317      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5318      * by running it inside an exception handler.
5319      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
5320      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
5321      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
5322      * <p>
5323      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
5324      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
5325      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
5326      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
5327      * <p>
5328      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5329      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
5330      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
5331      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
5332      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
5333      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
5334      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5335      * T target(A..., B...);
5336      * T handler(ExType, A...);
5337      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5338      *   try {
5339      *     return target(a..., b...);
5340      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
5341      *     return handler(ex, a...);
5342      *   }
5343      * }
5344      * }</pre></blockquote>
5345      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5346      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
5347      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
5348      * <p>
5349      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
5350      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
5351      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
5352      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
5353      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
5354      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
5355      * @param target method handle to call
5356      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
5357      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
5358      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
5359      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5360      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
5361      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
5362      *          not match in their return types and their
5363      *          corresponding parameters
5364      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5365      */
5366     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
5367                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
5368                                 MethodHandle handler) {
5369         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5370         MethodType htype = handler.type();
5371         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5372             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5373         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
5374             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
5375             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
5376         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
5377             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
5378         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
5379         if (handler == null) {
5380             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
5381         }
5382         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
5383     }
5384 
5385     /**
5386      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
5387      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
5388      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
5389      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
5390      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
5391      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
5392      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
5393      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
5394      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
5395      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5396      */
5397     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
5398         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5399             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5400         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
5401     }
5402 
5403     /**
5404      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
5405      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
5406      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
5407      * <p>
5408      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
5409      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
5410      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
5411      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
5412      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
5413      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
5414      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
5415      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
5416      * </ul>
5417      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
5418      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
5419      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
5420      * <p>
5421      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
5422      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
5423      * <p>
5424      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
5425      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
5426      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
5427      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
5428      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
5429      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
5430      * <p>
5431      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
5432      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
5433      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
5434      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
5435      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
5436      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
5437      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
5438      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
5439      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
5440      * <p>
5441      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
5442      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
5443      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
5444      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
5445      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
5446      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
5447      * <a id="astar"></a>
5448      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
5449      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
5450      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
5451      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
5452      * <p>
5453      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
5454      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
5455      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
5456      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
5457      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
5458      * <p>
5459      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
5460      * <a id="effid"></a>
5461      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
5462      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
5463      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
5464      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
5465      * that longest list.
5466      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
5467      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
5468      * <p>
5469      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
5470      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
5471      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
5472      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
5473      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
5474      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
5475      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
5476      * </ol>
5477      * <p>
5478      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
5479      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
5480      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
5481      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
5482      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
5483      * iteration variable type.
5484      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
5485      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
5486      * </ol>
5487      * <p>
5488      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
5489      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
5490      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
5491      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
5492      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
5493      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
5494      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
5495      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
5496      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
5497      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
5498      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
5499      * the "internal parameter list".
5500      * </ul>
5501      * <p>
5502      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
5503      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
5504      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
5505      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
5506      * type.
5507      * </ol>
5508      * <p>
5509      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
5510      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
5511      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
5512      * </ol>
5513      * <p>
5514      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
5515      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
5516      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
5517      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
5518      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
5519      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
5520      * </ol>
5521      * <p>
5522      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
5523      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
5524      * type.
5525      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
5526      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
5527      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
5528      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
5529      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
5530      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
5531      * loop return type.
5532      * </ol>
5533      * <p>
5534      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
5535      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
5536      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
5537      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
5538      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
5539      * pad out the end of the list.
5540      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
5541      * </ol>
5542      * <p>
5543      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
5544      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
5545      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
5546      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
5547      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
5548      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
5549      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
5550      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
5551      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
5552      * </ol>
5553      * <p>
5554      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
5555      * <ul>
5556      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
5557      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
5558      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
5559      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
5560      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
5561      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
5562      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
5563      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
5564      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
5565      * </ul>
5566      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
5567      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
5568      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
5569      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
5570      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
5571      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
5572      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
5573      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
5574      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
5575      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
5576      * <p>
5577      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
5578      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
5579      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
5580      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
5581      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
5582      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
5583      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
5584      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
5585      * (in argument order).
5586      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
5587      * returns {@code false}.
5588      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
5589      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
5590      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
5591      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
5592      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
5593      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
5594      * except by throwing an exception.
5595      * </ol>
5596      * <p>
5597      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
5598      * <ul>
5599      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
5600      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
5601      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
5602      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
5603      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
5604      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
5605      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
5606      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
5607      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
5608      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
5609      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
5610      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
5611      * </ul>
5612      * <p>
5613      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
5614      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
5615      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
5616      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5617      * V... init...(A...);
5618      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
5619      * V... step...(V..., A...);
5620      * R fini...(V..., A...);
5621      * R loop(A... a) {
5622      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
5623      *   for (;;) {
5624      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
5625      *       v = s(v..., a...);
5626      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
5627      *         return f(v..., a...);
5628      *       }
5629      *     }
5630      *   }
5631      * }
5632      * }</pre></blockquote>
5633      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
5634      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
5635      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
5636      *
5637      * @apiNote Example:
5638      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5639      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5640      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
5641      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
5642      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
5643      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
5644      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
5645      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
5646      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5647      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5648      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5649      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5650      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
5651      * }</pre></blockquote>
5652      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
5653      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5654      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5655      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
5656      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
5657      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
5658      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
5659      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5660      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
5661      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
5662      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
5663      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5664      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5665      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5666      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
5667      * }</pre></blockquote>
5668      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
5669      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5670      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5671      * static class FacLoop {
5672      *   final int k;
5673      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
5674      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
5675      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
5676      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
5677      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
5678      * }
5679      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
5680      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
5681      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5682      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
5683      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
5684      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5685      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5686      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5687      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
5688      * }</pre></blockquote>
5689      *
5690      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
5691      *
5692      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
5693      *
5694      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
5695      *
5696      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5697      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5698      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5699      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5700      * @since 9
5701      */
5702     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
5703         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
5704         loopChecks0(clauses);
5705 
5706         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
5707         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
5708         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
5709         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
5710 
5711         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
5712             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
5713             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
5714             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
5715             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
5716         });
5717 
5718         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
5719         final int nclauses = init.size();
5720 
5721         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
5722         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
5723         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
5724             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
5725             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
5726             if (in == null && st == null) {
5727                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
5728             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
5729                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
5730                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
5731             } else {
5732                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
5733             }
5734         }
5735         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
5736                 collect(Collectors.toList());
5737 
5738         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
5739         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
5740         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
5741 
5742         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
5743         // Step 1D: check other types.
5744         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
5745         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
5746                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
5747         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
5748         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
5749 
5750         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
5751         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
5752         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
5753         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
5754 
5755         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
5756         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
5757             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
5758             if (init.get(i) == null) {
5759                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
5760             }
5761             if (step.get(i) == null) {
5762                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
5763             }
5764             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
5765                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
5766             }
5767             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
5768                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
5769             }
5770         }
5771 
5772         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
5773         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
5774         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
5775         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
5776         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
5777         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
5778 
5779         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
5780                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
5781         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
5782                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
5783 
5784         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
5785     }
5786 
5787     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
5788         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
5789             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
5790         }
5791         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
5792             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
5793         }
5794         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
5795             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
5796         }
5797     }
5798 
5799     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
5800         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
5801             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
5802                     st.type().returnType());
5803         }
5804     }
5805 
5806     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
5807         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
5808         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
5809                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
5810                         map(MethodHandle::type).
5811                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
5812                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
5813                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
5814         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
5815     }
5816 
5817     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
5818         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
5819         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
5820     }
5821 
5822     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
5823         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
5824         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
5825         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
5826     }
5827 
5828     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
5829         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
5830                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
5831             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
5832                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
5833         }
5834     }
5835 
5836     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
5837         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
5838                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
5839             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
5840                     loopReturnType + ")");
5841         }
5842 
5843         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
5844             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
5845         }
5846         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
5847                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
5848             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
5849         }
5850     }
5851 
5852     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
5853         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
5854                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
5855             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
5856                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
5857         }
5858     }
5859 
5860     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
5861         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
5862             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
5863             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
5864             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
5865         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
5866     }
5867 
5868     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
5869         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
5870     }
5871 
5872     /**
5873      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
5874      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
5875      * <p>
5876      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
5877      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
5878      * evaluates to {@code true}).
5879      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
5880      * <p>
5881      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
5882      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
5883      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
5884      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
5885      * <p>
5886      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
5887      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
5888      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
5889      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
5890      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
5891      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
5892      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
5893      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
5894      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
5895      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
5896      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
5897      * additional state variable of the loop.
5898      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
5899      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
5900      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
5901      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
5902      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
5903      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
5904      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
5905      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
5906      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
5907      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
5908      * </ul>
5909      * <p>
5910      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
5911      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
5912      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
5913      * from the external parameter list.
5914      * </ul>
5915      * <p>
5916      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
5917      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
5918      * passed to the loop.
5919      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5920      * V init(A...);
5921      * boolean pred(V, A...);
5922      * V body(V, A...);
5923      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
5924      *   V v = init(a...);
5925      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
5926      *     v = body(v, a...);
5927      *   }
5928      *   return v;
5929      * }
5930      * }</pre></blockquote>
5931      *
5932      * @apiNote Example:
5933      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5934      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
5935      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
5936      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
5937      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
5938      *   zip.add(a.next());
5939      *   zip.add(b.next());
5940      *   return zip;
5941      * }
5942      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
5943      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
5944      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
5945      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
5946      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
5947      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
5948      * }</pre></blockquote>
5949      *
5950      *
5951      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
5952      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5953      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
5954      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
5955      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
5956      *     MethodHandle[]
5957      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
5958      *         varBody   = { init, body };
5959      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
5960      * }
5961      * }</pre></blockquote>
5962      *
5963      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
5964      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
5965      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
5966      *             above for other constraints.
5967      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
5968      *             See above for other constraints.
5969      *
5970      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
5971      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
5972      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
5973      *
5974      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
5975      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5976      * @since 9
5977      */
5978     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
5979         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
5980         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
5981         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
5982         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
5983         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
5984     }
5985 
5986     /**
5987      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
5988      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
5989      * <p>
5990      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
5991      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
5992      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
5993      * <p>
5994      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
5995      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
5996      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
5997      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
5998      * <p>
5999      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6000      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6001      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6002      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6003      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6004      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6005      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6006      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6007      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6008      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6009      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6010      * additional state variable of the loop.
6011      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6012      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6013      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6014      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6015      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6016      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6017      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6018      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6019      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6020      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6021      * </ul>
6022      * <p>
6023      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6024      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6025      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6026      * from the external parameter list.
6027      * </ul>
6028      * <p>
6029      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6030      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6031      * passed to the loop.
6032      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6033      * V init(A...);
6034      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6035      * V body(V, A...);
6036      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6037      *   V v = init(a...);
6038      *   do {
6039      *     v = body(v, a...);
6040      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6041      *   return v;
6042      * }
6043      * }</pre></blockquote>
6044      *
6045      * @apiNote Example:
6046      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6047      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6048      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6049      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6050      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6051      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6052      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6053      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6054      * }</pre></blockquote>
6055      *
6056      *
6057      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6058      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6059      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6060      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6061      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6062      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6063      *     return loop(clause);
6064      * }
6065      * }</pre></blockquote>
6066      *
6067      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6068      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6069      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6070      *             See above for other constraints.
6071      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6072      *             above for other constraints.
6073      *
6074      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6075      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6076      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6077      *
6078      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6079      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6080      * @since 9
6081      */
6082     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6083         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6084         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6085         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6086         return loop(clause);
6087     }
6088
