6089     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6090         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6091         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6092         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6093         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6094         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6095         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6096         if (returnType == void.class) {
6097             // OK
6098         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6099             // leading V argument missing => error
6100             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6101             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6102         } else {
6103             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6104         }
6105         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6106         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6107                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6108             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6109         }
6110         if (init != null) {
6111             MethodType initType = init.type();
6112             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6113                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6114                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6115             }
6116         }
6117     }
6118 
6119     /**
6120      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6121      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6122      * <p>
6123      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6124      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6125      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6126      * <p>
6127      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6128      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6129      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6130      * <p>
6131      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6132      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6133      * iteration variable.
6134      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6135      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6136      * <p>
6137      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6138      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6139      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6140      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6141      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6142      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6143      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6144      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6145      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6146      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6147      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6148      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6149      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6150      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6151      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6152      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6153      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6154      * additional state variable of the loop.
6155      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6156      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6157      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6158      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6159      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6160      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6161      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6162      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6163      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6164      * </ul>
6165      * <p>
6166      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6167      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6168      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6169      * from the external parameter list.
6170      * </ul>
6171      * <p>
6172      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6173      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6174      * arguments passed to the loop.
6175      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6176      * int iterations(A...);
6177      * V init(A...);
6178      * V body(V, int, A...);
6179      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6180      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6181      *   V v = init(a...);
6182      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6183      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6184      *   }
6185      *   return v;
6186      * }
6187      * }</pre></blockquote>
6188      *
6189      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6190      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6191      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6192      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6193      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6194      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6195      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6196      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6197      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6198      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6199      * }</pre></blockquote>
6200      *
6201      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6202      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6203      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6204      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6205      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6206      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6207      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6208      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6209      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6210      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6211      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6212      * }</pre></blockquote>
6213      *
6214      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6215      * as loop parameters:
6216      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6217      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6218      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6219      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6220      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6221      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6222      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6223      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6224      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6225      * }</pre></blockquote>
6226      *
6227      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6228      * to enforce a loop type:
6229      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6230      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6231      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6232      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6233      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6234      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6235      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6236      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6237      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6238      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6239      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6240      * }</pre></blockquote>
6241      *
6242      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6243      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6244      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6245      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6246      * }
6247      * }</pre></blockquote>
6248      *
6249      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6250      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6251      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6252      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6253      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6254      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6255      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6256      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6257      *             See above for other constraints.
6258      *
6259      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6260      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6261      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6262      *
6263      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6264      * @since 9
6265      */
6266     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6267         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6268     }
6269 
6270     /**
6271      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6272      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6273      * <p>
6274      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6275      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6276      * values of the loop counter.
6277      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6278      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6279      * <p>
6280      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6281      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6282      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6283      * <p>
6284      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6285      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6286      * iteration variable.
6287      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6288      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6289      * <p>
6290      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6291      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6292      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6293      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6294      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6295      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6296      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6297      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6298      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6299      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6300      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6301      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6302      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6303      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6304      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6305      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6306      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6307      * additional state variable of the loop.
6308      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6309      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6310      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6311      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6312      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6313      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6314      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6315      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6316      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6317      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6318      * to the external parameter list.
6319      * </ul>
6320      * <p>
6321      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6322      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6323      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6324      * from the external parameter list.
6325      * </ul>
6326      * <p>
6327      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6328      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6329      * arguments passed to the loop.
6330      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6331      * int start(A...);
6332      * int end(A...);
6333      * V init(A...);
6334      * V body(V, int, A...);
6335      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6336      *   int e = end(a...);
6337      *   int s = start(a...);
6338      *   V v = init(a...);
6339      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
6340      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6341      *   }
6342      *   return v;
6343      * }
6344      * }</pre></blockquote>
6345      *
6346      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6347      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6348      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6349      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
6350      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
6351      *     // the following semantics:
6352      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
6353      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
6354      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
6355      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6356      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
6357      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
6358      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6359      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6360      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
6361      *     }
6362      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6363      *     MethodHandle[]
6364      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6365      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6366      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6367      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6368      * }
6369      * }</pre></blockquote>
6370      *
6371      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
6372      *              See above for other constraints.
6373      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
6374      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6375      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6376      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6377      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6378      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6379      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6380      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6381      *             See above for other constraints.
6382      *
6383      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6384      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6385      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6386      *
6387      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6388      * @since 9
6389      */
6390     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6391         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
6392         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
6393         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
6394         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
6395         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
6396         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
6397         MethodHandle retv = null;
6398         if (returnType != void.class) {
6399             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6400             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6401             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
6402         }
6403         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6404         MethodHandle[]
6405             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6406             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6407             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6408         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6409     }
6410 
6411     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6412         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
6413         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
6414         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6415         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
6416         if (counterType != int.class) {
6417             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
6418             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
6419         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
6420             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
6421             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
6422         }
6423         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6424         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6425         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6426         // strip leading V value if present
6427         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6428         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6429             // argument list has no "V" => error
6430             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6431             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6432         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
6433             // missing I type => error
6434             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
6435             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6436         }
6437         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
6438         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
6439             // special case; take lists from end handle
6440             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
6441             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
6442         }
6443         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
6444         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6445             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
6446         }
6447         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
6448             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6449             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
6450         }
6451         if (init != null) {
6452             MethodType initType = init.type();
6453             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6454                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6455                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6456             }
6457         }
6458     }
6459 
6460     /**
6461      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
6462      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6463      * <p>
6464      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
6465      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
6466      * <p>
6467      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6468      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6469      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6470      * <p>
6471      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6472      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6473      * iteration variable.
6474      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6475      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6476      * <p>
6477      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6478      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6479      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
6480      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6481      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6482      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
6483      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6484      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6485      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6486      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
6487      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6488      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
6489      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
6490      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6491      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6492      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6493      * additional state variable of the loop.
6494      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6495      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6496      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6497      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6498      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6499      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6500      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6501      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
6502      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
6503      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
6504      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
6505      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6506      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6507      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
6508      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
6509      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
6510      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
6511      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
6512      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
6513      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
6514      * </ul>
6515      * <p>
6516      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
6517      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
6518      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
6519      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
6520      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
6521      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
6522      * <p>
6523      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6524      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6525      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6526      * from the external parameter list.
6527      * </ul>
6528      * <p>
6529      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6530      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
6531      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
6532      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6533      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
6534      * V init(A...);
6535      * V body(V,T,A...);
6536      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
6537      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
6538      *   V v = init(a...);
6539      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
6540      *     T t = it.next();
6541      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
6542      *   }
6543      *   return v;
6544      * }
6545      * }</pre></blockquote>
6546      *
6547      * @apiNote Example:
6548      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6549      * // get an iterator from a list
6550      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
6551      *   r.add(0, e);
6552      *   return r;
6553      * }
6554      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6555      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
6556      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
6557      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
6558      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
6559      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
6560      * }</pre></blockquote>
6561      *
6562      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
6563      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6564      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6565      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
6566      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6567      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6568      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
6569      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
6570      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
6571      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
6572      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
6573      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
6574      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
6575      *     }
6576      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
6577      *     MethodHandle[]
6578      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
6579      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
6580      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
6581      * }
6582      * }</pre></blockquote>
6583      *
6584      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
6585      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
6586      *                 See above for other constraints.
6587      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6588      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6589      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6590      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6591      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
6592      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6593      *             See above for other constraints.
6594      *
6595      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
6596      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
6597      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
6598      *
6599      * @since 9
6600      */
6601     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6602         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
6603         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6604         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
6605         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
6606         MethodHandle startIter;
6607         MethodHandle nextVal;
6608         {
6609             MethodType iteratorType;
6610             if (iterator == null) {
6611                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
6612                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
6613                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
6614             } else {
6615                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
6616                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
6617                 startIter = iterator;
6618             }
6619             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6620             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
6621 
6622             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
6623             try {
6624                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
6625                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
6626             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
6627                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
6628             }
6629         }
6630 
6631         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
6632         if (returnType != void.class) {
6633             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
6634             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
6635             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
6636             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
6637         }
6638 
6639         MethodHandle[]
6640             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
6641             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
6642         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
6643     }
6644 
6645     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6646         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6647         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6648         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6649         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
6650         // strip leading V value if present
6651         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6652         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6653             // argument list has no "V" => error
6654             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6655             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6656         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
6657             // missing T type => error
6658             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
6659             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6660         }
6661         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
6662         Class<?> iterableType = null;
6663         if (iterator != null) {
6664             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
6665             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
6666             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
6667                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
6668             }
6669             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
6670             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
6671                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
6672             }
6673             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
6674                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
6675                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
6676             }
6677         } else {
6678             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
6679                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
6680                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
6681                 // of Iterable
6682                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
6683                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
6684             } else {
6685                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
6686                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
6687                 // assignable to Iterable
6688                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
6689                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
6690                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
6691                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
6692                 }
6693             }
6694         }
6695         if (init != null) {
6696             MethodType initType = init.type();
6697             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6698                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
6699                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
6700             }
6701         }
6702         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
6703     }
6704 
6705     /*non-public*/
6706     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
6707         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
6708         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
6709         int[] order = new int[arity];
6710         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
6711         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
6712         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
6713         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
6714         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
6715         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
6716     }
6717 
6718     /**
6719      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
6720      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
6721      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
6722      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
6723      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
6724      * {@code try-finally} handle.
6725      * <p>
6726      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
6727      * The first is the exception thrown during the
6728      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
6729      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
6730      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
6731      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
6732      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
6733      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
6734      * <p>
6735      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
6736      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
6737      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
6738      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
6739      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
6740      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
6741      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
6742      * </ul>
6743      * <p>
6744      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
6745      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
6746      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
6747      * the cleanup.
6748      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6749      * V target(A..., B...);
6750      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
6751      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
6752      *   V result = (zero value for V);
6753      *   Throwable throwable = null;
6754      *   try {
6755      *     result = target(a..., b...);
6756      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
6757      *     throwable = t;
6758      *     throw t;
6759      *   } finally {
6760      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
6761      *   }
6762      *   return result;
6763      * }
6764      * }</pre></blockquote>
6765      * <p>
6766      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
6767      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
6768      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
6769      * <p>
6770      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
6771      * always throws.
6772      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
6773      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
6774      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
6775      * <p>
6776      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
6777      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
6778      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
6779      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
6780      * <p>
6781      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
6782      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
6783      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
6784      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
6785      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
6786      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
6787      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
6788      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
6789      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
6790      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
6791      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
6792      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
6793      *
6794      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
6795      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
6796      *
6797      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
6798      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
6799      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
6800      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
6801      *          not match in their return types and their
6802      *          corresponding trailing parameters
6803      *
6804      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
6805      * @since 9
6806      */
6807     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
6808         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
6809         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
6810 
6811         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
6812 
6813         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
6814         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
6815         // target parameter list.
6816         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
6817 
6818         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
6819         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
6820         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
6821 
6822         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
6823         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
6824     }
6825 
6826     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
6827         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
6828         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
6829             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
6830         }
6831         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
6832         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
6833             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
6834         }
6835         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
6836             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
6837         }
6838         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
6839         // target parameter list.
6840         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
6841         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
6842             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
6843                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
6844         }
6845     }
